We want a autotrophic network which learns the automata structure of a stochastic source. The signals is
piped through the input neurons which will grow a counter of occurences. When the occurences become large, 
they will birth children, representing dependent events, joint distributions. By the growth of the neurons,
the deeper neurons will necessarily be smaller, but frequently occuring subsequences will result in
considerable growth. The sizes of children can be normalised to get frequency/probability. We need some notion
of well-known and not well-known subsequences. There is a difference between depth reach and unfamiliarity.
For learning, depth reach will be a positive thing, while unfamiliarity will bad. The unfamiliary should maybe
used to change the structure of the network in some way..

The main ketone used in ketosis is the BHB and it is a precursor to brain-derived neurotropic factor BDNF. The
article https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5913738/ describes Intermittent metabolic switching
between ketone- and glucose-based metabolism either through time-resticted fasting or alternate day fasting
which has been studied extensively in rats. Intermittent metabolic switching induces dendritic growth in the
hippocampus, which is a brain area related to the relation between short-term and long-term memory and
spatial cognition, and studies show how the functionality of the hippocampus is improved in intermittent fasting
a term which they use for both TRF and ADF.

31-08-19-13-02
What is an epiphany?

Epiphanies are common and even characteristic phenomena on psychoactive drugs like cannabis and psychedelics. 
What is an epiphany? An epiphany is a thought that to the subject appears to be novel, important and furthermore
it has the quality of being revealed instead of constructed, that is, it is seems to have been present but 
only out of view. From this revelatory characteristic it is natural for subject to feel that not only is the
thought but that it is just as impressing that the thought have not been obvious already.

In relation to this obviousness it is natural to ask whether the epiphany has only an apparent novelty so that
the thought has appeared before but has not been captured the attention of the subject to the same degree. If 
this is the case the idea that some drugs lead to epiphanies should not be viewed as resulting from an 
increased computational power or more simply increased creativity in the most immediate sense of the word.
Instead there is a transformation of the evaluating function, the attribution of importance to phenomena 
in the mind mediated by alteration of neurotransmitter activity.

As of now we have treated an epiphany as a special type of thought as in a structure of meaning. How does this 
to relate to more advanced changes in what can only be called cognitive behavior? A subject on a psychedelic 
drug might have a pervasive impression that a very general fear or limitation has been lifted or suspended,
giving rise to specific epiphanies whose linguistic representation will be that a specific situation or person 
should not be feared, but still spanning a more general notion. Here we are again left to speculation. Many 
aspects of affect like fear involve low-level regions of the brain even though epiphanies surely belong to 
higher cortical regions since they often involve complex semantic and conceptual representations of the self 
in relation to social existence.

It might be that the drugs cause a relative deactivation of neural networks related to fear and that the effect
is that any thoughts which occur will now appear in an altered emotional context which results in an altered 
perception of the situation represented by the thought, in many cases a more positive or even rational view.

I am going to try to write for 15 minutes. I am reading very sporadically about neuroscience. I think that I 
am perhaps considering whether I should try to get a career in it, even though I have until now been quite
sure that bioinformatics was the way. The argument for being focused on bioinformatics is that it has a much
more clear application to health and thus has more ethical power. The data which is dealt with in bioinformatics
is also much vaster and diverse than what can be found in neuroscience. It might be possible to combine the two
or to get expertise in the bioinformatics and then transition to computational neuroscience later. I can see
that in both bioinformatics and neuroscience I am not so much interested in the application of the tools, that
is analysing some dataset but to develop new methods of investigation, algorithms and models to use. In that
way I am staying close to the mathematics but still in an applied way in which mathematics and computation shows
its beauty in the application to natural systems. The notion of criticality, complexity and dynamic behavior is
very interesting in relation to neural systems even though it is probably also present in molecular systems.
Self-organising behavior and modularity is likewise. I just found a dissertation about the effect of meditation
and mind-wandering on long range temporal correlations in EEG time signals.

Yesterday afternoon I went for a walk and contemplated the causal or conditioned nature of all the phenomena I
saw, how I had common ancestors, common grand-grand-... parents with every person I saw and every plant, and
the reasons why something appeared in my consciousness exactly in that place and at that moment and with exactly
those properties. But it seems that some of the facts which are contemplated in the casual, conditional or
reason-based nature are weird. 'There is a reason that person is walking right there right now'. Causes for
that person include all of his environmental conditioning, epigenetic influences, food, environment, genes,
his parents and all of his evolutionary history. All of his social causes, there is a reason why he lives in
the same town as me, if he has a job there, there is a reason why he got that job, there is a reason why he
accepted that job, there is a reason why the company exists, there is a reason why the town we are in exists.
He also had intentions leading to him walking there right now. It is not clear what causes are. If reversibility
exists, if no information is lost, I can only say that actions happened prior to his being here and that they
are continuous with his being here. If information is lost and reversibility does not exist then there could
be multiple time series leading to the same moment in a coherent manner.

og gerne ville at det skulle være meget godt. Så jeg tror jeg havde lidt for store ambitioner på gruppens
vejne, mens jeg også tror at Rasmus og Carl var for lidt engagerede. Jeg tror altså at vi alle er ansvarlige
for at jeg synes det på nogle tidspunkter var meget utilfredsstillende. Da jeg åbnede op til aller sidst, da
vi skulle til at lave eksamensprojekt var det imidlertid meget godt. Jeg tror at jeg tænker, at den periode
jeg var i til sidst gav mig overskud, men at jeg ikke kan forvente at være i en sådan tilstand gennem året.
Det er et generelt tema: Der findes objektive stressorer, og nogle af dem kan klares ved psyko-spirituelle
tilgange, men det betyder ikke at man ikke skal være interesseret i at minimere de objektive stressorer.
Derfor tror jeg det bedste ville være, om jeg fandt en studiegruppe, hvor der ikke var samme stress på, så
jeg kan have det godt, når jeg ikke er helt oppe på den hvide mindfulness-hest. Da Lauritz besøge mig i går
talte han om at jeg nok godt kunne være i gruppe med ham. Jeg føler at en af faktorerne, hvis jeg skulle vælge
mellem de to muligheder ville være dygtighed i gruppemedlemmerne vs forbindelse. Jeg synes Rasmus og Carl er
meget dygtige selvom det ikke altid kommer til udtryk, og jeg tror det er vigtigt at jeg er sammen med folk
jeg synes er dygtige og som jeg er på samme niveau med. Som sagt har jeg det egentlig også fint socialt sammen
med Rasmus og Carl. I Lauritz' gruppe arbejder de andre også, og Lauritz siger selv at han nok kommer til at
bruge meget tid sammen med sin kæreste Laura, så måske ville der ikke være så meget forskel der heller. Jeg
ved heller ikke om jeg ville klinge bedre med den gruppe end med de andre.

29-08-19-16-22
Har haft besøg af Lauritz her 11-15.30.

When I see an object in my environment I am seeing something 'there', but I know that it will take time for
the light or the sound to travel from the destination to my sense organs and into my brain. If I imagine my
consciousness to be related to the brain then what I perceive as 'now there' is actually 'now here' and
'before there'. I have the impression that I am living in a specific moment of time which is distinct from
the past and future, even though I have no idea why it is this point in time I am experiencing instead of
another. I perceive only a limited part of the world and thus I have only limited information about the
state of the universe. If the universe is reversibly deterministic, then if I were able to perceive everything
in the now I would be able to see the past and the future. I have some kind of speculation that this limited
character of my experience is related to qualia. Yet, I do not even have a clear notion of the possibility of
perceiving everything: Which kinds of universes support the possibility that a part of the universe can know
the whole of the universe? A subsystem knowing the system. What does it mean to know, what does it mean to
have information about something else? I know that the vibrations of the hair on my arm right now is dependent
upon conditions in the wind which is dependent upon conditions, but how much information can be gained by a
precise 'measurement' of these vibrations? How much information exists at the shore of my body? If this
information is not the full picture, which I doubt that it is, does the limited information which is present
still set a definite probability distribution on the state of the remaining universe. Is there anything which
is certain given this information, or will it all be under probability distributions? If I am seeing the object
'now here' it is because it was 'there before'. Even though it is a good guess, I have no understanding of
the mechanism by which conscious experience should arise from the 'now here' of electrical activity in my brain,
and it could open up the possibility of hypothesising that this consciousness does not exist at a moment in time,
that I am not perceiving a moment in time but instead am perceiving a moment back to the origin of the universe
in a limited manner. I am very interested in an articulation, no matter how speculative, of the idea that
perception and inference is fundamentally linked, that the perception of a pattern, an object, is dependent
upon the prior structure which makes the perception possible, but not in the same way Kant describes
transcendental subjectivity. The perceiving structure, the brain perhaps, is itself a product of a kind of
process of perception, evolution, even though this process of perception is vastly different than the one
existing in human organisms.

27-08-19-13-04
Der er gået lang tid siden jeg skrev i loggen sidste gang. Jeg har ikke brugt computeren så meget
i sommerferien. Jeg har skrevet lidt i hånden, og det kan være jeg skriver det over på et tidspunkt.
Hovedtemaet i min sommerferie har været meditation, både samadhi og vipassana. Jeg har holdt pause
fra tanker om datalogi og er kun lige begyndt at læse op her for nyligt. Jeg har det generelt rigtig
godt, men jeg har lidt mangel på energi her i dag, og jeg tror det er derfor jeg har åbnet loggen igen.
Jeg har været i Aarhus fra torsdag til søndag; jeg var sammen med Jørgen, Monica, Steven, Emma, til
fest hos Laura Lentz, Noah og andre fra Testrup og besøgte Oskar Vedel søndag, inden jeg tog tilbage
og var så sammen med Peter i går. Jeg var sammen med både Caroline og Nanna onsdag, inden jeg tog til
Aarhus. Jeg følte at jeg havde overskud til at være social, og at det ville være godt for mig at blive
stimuleret på den måde, og at det ville være godt at nå at være sammen med folk i sommerferien, da jeg
nok får mindre tid til det, når studiet starter. Overskuddet til at være social får en ind i selve
konteksten, hvor energien så bliver brugt og omformer mit nervesystem, der derved er blevet tilpasset.
Denne ændring kræver tid og ro. Derfor er jeg lidt i tvivl om, hvor hårdt jeg skal arbejde på at
repetere matematik til MASD kurset, for der er jo også andre ting jeg gerne vil, som jeg ikke kan lave
så meget når jeg starter igen. Især meditation, men også generel læring af emner relateret til meditation,
neurovidenskab og lignende. Jeg tror godt jeg kan mærke at jeg ikke har trænet i en uge nu, men her er
jeg på samme måde i tvivl om, hvor meget jeg skal stresse min krop. Hele konceptet om stress er ekstremt
interessant, og det virker som om det kan stikke meget dybt. Det var noget af det jeg skrev om i starten
af sommerferien på tekst. Jeg fik 12 til den mundtlige eksamen i softwareudvikling og tog ned på Christania
og røg med god samvittighed. Jeg tænkte at jeg ville bruge det som en måde at tænke på, hvad jeg skulle
lave i sommerferien. Jeg tror lidt at jeg konkluderede, at det ville være godt at være meget derhjemme og
bruge tid på at træne, lave mad og lære ting jeg ikke normalt havde tid til. Det virkede for mig som den
mest rationelle måde at bruge tid, i stedet for at tage et sted hen på ferie, og at det mest var
sociale normer om, hvad en sommerferie skal være, der forhindrede én i at gøre dette. Jeg brugte også
en del dage i slutten af juni på bare at være derhjemme, og slappe af, træne, prøve at sove kun på
topmadras og lave one meal a day (OMAD). Det var godt ikke at skulle være bundet af præstationsfølelsen,
at der var noget man skulle lave. Jeg begyndte også gradvist at meditere mere de dage. Undervejs tænkte
jeg, at det måske ville være kedeligt bare at være det samme sted hele ferien, og at det bare var et par
dage det var godt at køre den som jeg gjorde da. Jeg tog hjem til Gjern en uge, jeg tror ikke de andre
havde ferie. Jeg begyndte at meditere meget mere på det tidspunkt, og læste Shinzen Young og Daniel Ingram,
var på cykeltur med farfar og Theodor Boas. Jeg tog hjem fra Gjern igen og begyndte at meditere mere
intensivt, lidt som en slags retræte. Jeg tror jeg lærte meget og kom ind i rimelig kontinuerlig mindfulness
og havde en dyb ro. Jeg gjorde det i en uge. Jeg havde ikke nogen fast teknik, det var meget en blanding af
koncentration, noting, opmærksomhed på brystet, hovedet og lignende. Jeg gik også med nogle mere tekniske
tanker om meditation, der holdt mig lidt centreret på trods af at jeg også blev lidt skør i hovedet og havde
svært ved at balancere i det. Jeg mener at problemet er, at kontinuerlig meditation gør at man ikke får nok
tid til at reflektere analytisk over hvad der foregår, og derfor svækker sin kritiske sans. Jeg skriver
noterne ind nu, på det tidspunkt hvor de hører til.

10-07-19-12-00
I am on the path of liberation and purfication, where all defilements, all reactivity is to be destroyed
and eliminated from my existence. I have found that at my torso there is a complex of suffering which is
activated very clearly when I am lost in reactivity and mindlessness. I have no hesitation on this path,
what will get me to the destination the fastest will be my mode of movement, my vehicle. Yesterday it was
pain in the legs, I learned how to see the movement, the flow. I imagined the heatmap of my bodily
pleasantness and unpleasantness. I tried to see what purification looks like, how it feels. I believe I
succeeded at bit. The pain in the legs was a phenomenon to which the sword of equanimity could be applied,
and it resulted in a profound experiential insight into no-self. I have had difficulty in understanding how
to look for no-self in phenomena, compared to the more intuitive characteristics of impermanence and
unsatisfactoriness. It seems to me that equanimity eluminates anatta and vice verca. When faced with an
unpleasant sensation, especially an intense one, equanimity as an act is an act of release, an act of delving
into the sensation without resistance. By not resisting, one is letting go of control, and it is control which
I found to be the hallmark of self. All phenomena, both internal and external, in any sense sphere, is outside
my control, the sensation comes without me causing it, it goes without me causing it. This does not mean that
the phenomena are fully random, that there is no pattern. On the contrary there is great structure and
predictability and this further underlines the lack of any self. The only thing the self can do is to resist:
Resist the coming of unpleasantness, resist the going of pleasantness. The self in this sense, is an ecology
of microreactions which will have to be pulverized in order to get to a state where consciousness is free and
luminous, where phenomena appear in consciousness completely free from restraint. And so it is that I can
infer by feeling that a huge part of this ecology of reactions is to be identified and uprotted in my torso.
I do not however have the necessary samadhi to reap the rewards which I want, so I will have to invest in the
practice of concentration, which will surely pay off.

I had a good one hour sit where I started by trying to be mindful of the chest, but the result was not as clear
as earlier today where there was a more concentrated ball of sensations in the solar plexus. I think I got
quite agitated because I reasoned at one point that I was not accepting the current sensations as they were,
I had tried to force some other darker sensations to appear. I began to make a choiceless meditation inspired
by the no-self meditation yesterday. A painful sensation in my foot was deconstructed using a kind of thought-
led mediation in which I tried to isolate the specific small point which was painful. However, all the individual
sensations were either neural or pleasant. This invenstigation increased the clarity of the field, the fidelity
of the picture, and resulted in a stronger mindfulness of anicca, where the pain was a strong flow. The pain
lost its painfulness after this investigation, and then it returned again later, but still the investigation
had the same conclusion, although there was less concentration present to perform it satisfactorily. I think
I have gained a small insight into emptiness and there is also a phenomena of voices and bird sounds outside
my window being more composite and anicca-revealing, and experience I previously identified with LSD. Lastly,
I had a nice experience of feeling a similarity between the pain in the foot and the pleasant sensations in my
face, which I have also experienced on LSD. Bird sounds which I normally regard as unpretty and disturbing now
have a kind of synesthetic richness to them which resonate pleasantly in my skull. How many frustrating
sensations will be uncovered in their beauty of the path of purification?

11-07-19-12-00
I have been making one hour sits in which I can feel anicca in my legs and feet. I sometimes, when enough
clarity is present, feel like I can see a kind of vortex out of which all this energy is pouring. I feel that
by centering on these intense locations I make the most progress. It is weird that I am not sure what exactly
I am doing, there is not really a formula for equanimity, it seems like I am just trying to delve in with a
bare knowing. It is not really awareness of arising and passing of phenomena but more an awareness of flow
and energy. In this sit I experienced twistings of the foot and legs. They come when I obtain a respectable
focus on the locus and they appear for a couple of seconds after which I try to relax, in order not to
injure my knees. It is much easier to be equanimous about intensity in my feet than in my legs. When the pain
is in my feet I am not worrying about injuring myself because I can see clearly that it is not coming from a
physical problem there, in the knees, however, this is not so easy. According to a thread on DharmaOverground
where a guy reports tremors, which I also experiences as a shaking quite violently of the whole upperbody in
one case, this is probably the vipassana-nana of Arising and Passing. I am not sure my knowledge of mindfulness
has much to do with arising and passing currently, as already noted, but I do not care much since I am
relatively confident that I am making adequate progress using this approach.

I don't want to reflect too much on the meaning of all of this because it seems that the important thing seems
to be to continue pushing forward towards further libration. Still, I believe that on the retreat in Java, one
of the problems was that I was not at all articulating my thoughts and it just ended up being a total half-
psychotic mess, so I will make a few notes. The nervous system is clearly involved in this and I believe that
the model of neural networks sheds some light on the process: As one is delving into the territory, one is faced
with pattern recognitions which are always present in any sensory signal processing, but which is now being
revealed in a more distilled form. For example I had when trying to sleep tonight at one point a strong feeling
of 'spideriness'. I am less afraid of spiders than the average person, but where from does this genral fear
arise? I have a vision of the spider's venom as a bery high-pitched tone penetrating the spine as a pure horror.
There is uglyness and unpleasantness in many phenomena because there is some recognition of the horrific
nightmares to which they are ever so slightly similar. When practicing vipassana the sensations become more
detailed but also one becomes more affectively responsive to these stimuli. This gives the practitioner the
possibility of applying even more equanimity to these phenomena also. It is important that one does not become
attracted to the feeling of psychedelic richness in phenomena but remember to be equanimous to pleasant
sensations also. I think this is one of my weaknesses, because I have developed attachment to the psychedelic
experience which is very similar to this. It is so similar that this is a clear point of departure if one wanted,
as I do, to understand this path of libration in neuroscientific terms.

12-07-19-12-00
Yesterday I made a one hour sit where I again focused the attention on the leg or rather foot pain. This again
resulted in twistings and cringing but no large shaking. I tried just for the experiment no to relax after a
few seconds and this resulted in an upwards movement of my knee, a bending back of my upper body and a springing
of my leg out of its bent position, instead just pointing straight ahead. The same thing happened with my other
feet [sic]. I found it rediculous and though [sic] that such a thing could not be a part of meditation since
strong determination is a thing and in a meditation hall there could be another person meditating in front of me.
I stopped the session to find more information. It is called kryas [sic] and it is normal but one should not
follow through with the forces driving them. One person had found them to originate in aversion. Generally one
should try to find out where they are coming from. I tried to sit again and now I had the perception that the
pain was just as signal that some part of the system did not like the position. At some point I reasoned that
it might just be my body trying to reject the sitting position which I have after all been sitting in much more
these couple of days than recently. I changed to the chari and afterwards I also had a good one hour with
concentration of breath.

I think I became quite discouraged by the kryas, thinking that I did something wrong, especially because I read
it being a result of a strongly concentrated meditation while my concentration had been not so good. Perhaps I
had developed attachment to the potential of doing a lot of purification through that pain and then it just
resultet in what looks like a messed up nervous system. So I thought that perhaps I am not going the right way.
Today I will work hard on developing my concentration on breath by using positive reinforcement of catching
thoughts and staying with the breath.

I made a session with anapanasati where I tried to develop equanimity when I found out I had forgot the breath
instead of judging myself. This resulted in a nice and peaceful session. Afterwards, I went for a walk with

about oneness arise. Sometimes doubt arose about me being misled by normal stomach discomfort but I use the

I feel very confused, sad even. I feel like mindfulness has left me. I felt som many things in my upper body, my
torso, but now I am less aware than before and I am unsure whether I am staying on the path. I am going for a
walk again with noting. I am not strong enough to do no-self right now.

I became encouraged again after watching a video with Shinzen Young and another man. The man had experienced

purification, of bhanga, dissolution. Even though the man spoke of great terros, which Shinzen said only some

I started the sit with the intention of continuing with solar plexus but I found that the intensity was greater
in the middle of the head so I explored that. It was/is much clearer that it is not pain but just intensity and
the flow it generates in the head is very pleasant so that makes me associate the intensity with pleasure even

is a strong acidic sensation on my tongue and the very thin reptilian sensations in the gum are also similar.
I did not have good concentration but I had good equanimity, completely forgiving each mind wandering. The
implatience was very strong again and I looked at the timer both 12 and 3 minutes before I was done. I am still in
a "state" which is similar.

13-07-19-12-00
Wet dream.

I went for a morning walk where I thought about processes after having insight into the processual character of
a duck swimming in the water spreading waves in the water. There are sources of signals such as a fly buzzing
around me. It emits sound and light and smell and so on. The sound is simply the pressure in air. No movement
can happen by an animal without the emission of a signal with a structure revealing information about the larger
pattern which it is. There are some signals which are emitted to the benefit such as bird sounds and some which
are not emitted for benefit such as the closing and opening of its eyes, which is presumably neutral. A sound
might have both beneficial and unbeneficial consequences. I think Deleuze and Guattari, Guattari especially, is
thinking a lot about spontaneous assembly of ecological systems. A sound action pattern evolves in one mind for
one purpose but has the effect of causing another recognition-response pair in another. This is the interlinking
mechanism of nature, its creativity. I tried to use nothing with 'fast' and 'slow' for processes. There are
processes such as a car driving in which change is easy to detect. There are trees which grow slowly and will
only move by wind, but if I am moving there is still change which can be noticed. I do not know the tree which
contains so much energy as evident by burning, I only receive some small amount and a finite number of bits
enter my nervous system.

The path of purification is surely a process of transformation of the nervous system. In each sensory event
there is information which the nervous system will process. There are patterns and structure to identify and
the energy will cascade through the system. There are cases where the procssing will end rather quickly, fx
seeing and identifying as tree. There are patterns which are more complex which result in further release of
energy throughout the torso in terms of emotions. I believe that in practicing mindfulness, we are undergoing
a process where we will generally let the information flow more, meaning our response to stimuli will be greater,
will involve more affect. This process can be intense because it is literally involving a higher intensity on
the nervous system. The usual response is a kind of blocking of the information where we only want to take part
of the picture. However, the information is not deleted, instead it is trapped in the system as potential. The
proble is that this means taht a later sensory vent will release some of the information because there is some
statistical similarity, but now information related to an old event is released for processing in an event which
is only partially similar. This reduces functionality because the cognition is non-optimal. In this case blocking
might again happen and now information from two different events will be mixed together because the sound was
misunderstood as somewhat like the first and because of the aversion to the first some information in the second
goes with it. All of this is just modelling, we do not know, but again it is worth thinking about in order not
to be confused and make hypotheses which are more less likely. By practicing non-reactivity and equanimity as
a reponse to sensory events we will first need the attention and concentration needed to identify a sensory
event as such at some level of granularity, gross or subtle. When this has been archieved, every moement is a
chance to release potential energy which is copresent with the actual stimuli. One will look closely at the
sensorial data and see the association made in the mind and the feelings present as a dynamics in the boyd. The
important part is to not react and to allow what is a miscognition of the sensorial data to flow out through the
system in an entropic process where its effects are diminished and released. By doing sitting meditation where
stimuli are limited we can almost identify the pressure from the potential energy without the need for a sensorial
event to release it. By just holding attention on the solar plexus or the middle of the head I have found that
there to be a strong intensity. Again the whole deal is to release the infomration by non-reactive, concentrated
attention. It is also helpful to practice an awareness of how there is a release in the larger nervous system
when attending to these intense points. The released flow can be pleasant and it is a means for imporivng aware-
ness of the body but it might also be an obstacle which removes focus from the area of intensity. I believe that
the more you focus on the area of intensity, the faster you release the information. The third noble truth of
the end of suffering can be formulated in this model as the fact that there is a finite number of bits stored
behind these walls, a finite number of joules of potential energy. This is encouragin to me because is shows the
end goal to be quite specific and the means to be clear. The high concentration will result in high bitrate or
high number of watts and this will naturally feel painful. It is important to remind oneself when the intensity
is strong that it is not physical pain but a more cognitive phenomenon, it is fear and trauma leaving the system.
Experiencing the release as something physical is the alternative to experiencing it as a feverish nightmare.

The head is quite intense but I think it is starting to become more dynamic in the entirety of the head even
though there is still a central area of intensity. I became quite discouraged, sad even, by the thought that
I could be doing something wrong and not staying on the path of purification but instead fucking up my nervous
system with some weird kundalini shit. I am right now more optimistic. I will stay mindful of whatever is
happening, knowing and seeing the phenomena to be changing and impersonal. This is bhanga, my dissolution and
redemption. Let it come.

some time which is relieving. I am experiencing my first episode of frustration and tiredness now, though I
should probabily just let it be anatta. 

25-07-19-12-00
Meditation on the six sense spheres reveal phenomena. Insight meditation asks us to decompose the phenomena in
order to reveal the empiness of the phenomena, to reveal its lack of fundamentality. This can be done by
contemplating the arising and passing of the appearacne in consciousness or contemplation of the causla character
of the appearance: There is a reason why I hear the sound of a dog barking, there is an unseens cause (unseen
for me). There is also a reductionistic act of penetration and decomposition which is linked to clarity. The
breath as a whole is divided into in and out breath, then the in and out breaths are divided individually
(recursively) into sequences of sensations temporally. These sesnations can be studied spatially: Not only do
they have a position, they are extended in tactile space, they have a form. The form can be examined as large
or small, intense or weak.

LSD made me interested in patterns. It seemed to me that they were fundamental but overlooked in their ontological
importance. The Gestalt principles seem trivial until one understands how far cognition can go from pattern
recognition. What is a pattern? For the purpose of practice it is anything in which there are multiple things
which are similar. The lines on this page forms a pattern of lines, but the lines are themselves patterns because
they are similar across the page. Polynomial of degree one. A tree forms a patern by likeness of the branches and
the likeness of the leaves which consist of only more patterns. By making noting meditation on 'pattern' one can
come to appreciate the great role patterns play. Where there is perception of some thing which is carved out
from the large sea of sense data it is because the brain has identified a pattern so one might try to contempate
what pattern has actually been identified. A black spot on the road is a pattern by likeness of color in
proximity.

It is clear that the sense data at each moment has an entropy which is far from minimal. Maximal entropy would
be a total randomness; the audible sphere would be pure white noise and the visual space would be a random
flicker of colored dots forming no patterns. That the entropy is low means that there is order, patternenss and
predictability. Some patterns are easier to identify that others, hold more infomration than others. Kolmogorov
complexity is the size of the algorithm which can produce the data or object and is thus the abstract theoretical
limit of how much it can be compressed. Any pattern is thus filled with redundancy.

We can wonder how the mind reacts to high and low complexity or entropy. Since the mind serves an organism which
will survive by information from the environment, it will prefer to have an understadning of that environment,
to make sense of the sense data and use that to predict what might happen to it in order to avoid death.
High entropy will then mean that there is difficulty in understadning the structure while low is predictable.
Predictability would not necessarily correlate with safety. Something could be predictably unsafe.

What would this technical perspective say to the notion that meeting the unknown requires courage? It is as if
though the human organism can choose to avoid the high entropy by closing down the processing of data by
perceptual labeling and thinking. By stopping at the level of a concept one will be free from having to account
for details in the data which might have high entropy. I claim that an unpleasant bird sound has elements which
do not fit the model which cognition uses to cognize it.

Mindfulness is the voluntary acceptance of higher than normal entropy in sense objects. By not believing you
already have a sufficient model of what the breath is, what walking feels like, details will be revealed which
are not explained by the current model which the neural networks constitute.

Then there is also the domain of abstract algebra with symmetries and how this is related to patterns and
information. A pattern is a symmetry.

Mindfulness as willful suspension of perceptual or conceptual judgement forces the power of neural cognition to
take the data as new evidence and adjust the priors for the model. This is the enlightenment factor of
investigation. The meditator should not forcefully apply investigation other than maintaining the natural
process of neural change and letting the change be sufficiently general by contemplating the three
characteristics. This is in order to avoid overfitting. As the process unfolds, entropy falls, one bcomes more
comfortable with what was previously uncertain and the energy expended is lowered, releasing energy. This
energy should be transmuted into effort when one loses the concentrated mindful state where investigation
happens. This effort is energy and joy, happiness which is needed for the work of being in high entropy territory.
But I will let happiness be joined with a more peaceful tranquility which supports equanimity. Equanimity is the
actual factor which supports the honest, non-reactive bare knowing of mindfulness. So the cycle continues until
we are done.

19-06-19-12-00
Følgende er skrevet efter jeg har fået sommerferie og inden jeg tog til Gjern første gang.

Human beings have concepts about phenomena, they will categorise parts of the field of perception, and thereby
view reality as consisting of objects of various classes. It is a very common philosophical point that in some
sense then, the objects are not real, because they are projections of the mind onto the perceived environment.
Still however, the categorisations are not arbitrary, they are based on similarities and reasonings which might
nok be perfect or optimal but still not arbitrary. If I look at a room with a chari, then I will directly have
the experience that there is a chair; I will not look at some sense data of light and start thinking about
separating some of the colors from others and computing the shape with some memory of other shapes and
visualising how some other chair might look if rotated. All of this processing, however the technical details
of cognition, have already occured as the chair appears in consciousness. This does not mean that my inner voice
says 'There is a chair there', it will be unarticulated in thought and instead be a part of a more general
model of my current environment, which will be important for the ways I think about possibilities of activity
in space.

How have these concepts been constructed? It will not need to be a language-dependent process, because we can
easily imagine other animals which do not have the same linguistic and abstract thinking capacities as us,
which will still treat reality as consisting of objects. The dog running for a log of wood for example. There
is no doubt that there is some aspect of the dog's intelligent cognition in which the log of wood is similar to
other logs of wood and it is only a matter of degree of intelligence which will determine whether the logs lying
on the ground on the ground will be put into connection with the trees. Most behavioral activity seems to be
independent of linguistic concepts in the sense of requiring them. I see it also as one of the lessons of moment-
to-moment mindfulness that much less thought is needed than one might intuitively think. Personally, my experience
is that language thought is mostly relevant for action when it comes to longer term planning. However, longer
term planning is almost always something which is linked to social interaction or in some way engaging with
society and intersubjective enterprises. All superindividual structures are almost without exceptions underpinned
by language structures which allow these complex structures to exist. It is a relevant point that just as language
forms a pinnacle of abstract intelligence within each individual which allows for advanced problem solving and
modelling of problems and solutions, so this power is also expressed in the social structures which depend on
the capacities. When characterising such things as a business, a vacation, a meeting, a store, one ned to accept
that even though these may be analysed from the perspective of assemblages and networks, the structure of these
assemblages are fully dependent on the computational capacities of human language which enables the conception
and coordination of these superhuman structures.

All perceived signals have a physical basis no matter whether they are occuring close in time at some point
outside the organism as the birds making sounds outside my window which I do not expect to be a hallucination
or the tune on my mind which is coming from the brain and has its basis in memory. My reflection is on time.
When does a conscious awareness of a signal occur? Concentration as a meditational exercise wit han object
will be the practice of asserting "one's" attention at this object to the exclusion of both extragenic and
intragenic signals, thoughts and perceptions. A loud external noise will have higher capacity to disrupt
concentration, and here we will have to ask whether it is possible to block this signal. I believe that people
who can enter deep jhanas can do this. One would then be in the right to ask what happens to this otherwise
distracting signal. It has a certain amplitude, a certain power or energy in a physical sense and the only
way to block a sound wave is to put up some barrier which will quite literally absorb the wave in some way.
The wave will meet some material which will be impacted by the wave, but this material is so strong that it is
a bad medium for the wave and so the information and energy is dying out as it flows in the medium and entering
smaller levels of vibration as if though settling in the material. This is a process of entropy. The waves
coming in the water in the oceans against the rock seems to die off but it is very well understood by all of us
that a miniscule erosion is happening.

One could put forth the hypothesis that a strong concentration will need the equivalent of a sound proof wall
within the neurological structure. If we do not believe that the signal can be magically stopped, then by
diconnecting the usual pathway by which sound enters consciousness will have to mean that the signal is
passing some other way. It will not take a deaf person any energy to ingore sounds, however. Here we can imagine
some part of the nervous system being broken in such a way that the information is lost in a thermodynamical
"wasting" process somewhere. This seems to be a sufficient argument to disprove the other argument. Now instead
the question becomes, how does experiences concentrators modulate what should probably be called the excitability
of the parts of the chain?

We can imagine in accordance with preliminary research that the default mode network is a functional network
of larger groups of neurons which play an important role in self-reference. Even though the ability to perceive
oneself as a person among others is emblematic of human intelligence, it is also obvious that this capactiy is 
also deeply problematic in cases where such exciations and activity leads to anxiety and general rumination
problems which are present in depression. Networks even though abstracted, eventually consist of neurons with
a metabolism. The heightened activity in this or other hypothetical networks related to self, would thus mean
that there is an increased process of energy release. The energy activity in the network will be regulated by
complex processes and so the ability to consciously or unconsciously regulate activity in these networks are of
course very interesting. First there is a general aspect of regulation which is quite non-intuitive, at least 
for me, especially when it comes to self-regulation. It is simply a fact that at some levels there a homeostatic 
processes in the organism which are indeed carried out by the system itself. But what does it mean for a system
to have information about itself? There is no way to have a system which has complete transparency of its own
state, because such information about state needs a physical correlate and so we would enter some kind of
Russell's paradox. Only by the concept of feed in which the output of some part of the network is channeled
as input to some part prior in the chain, will the network have information about its own state, and this will
happen without introducing any aspect of self-transcendence of the network. The idea of a prior state is a bit 
hard to handle, however: Do we need to think of networks as chains? If there is no feedback, then yes, we will
have to view it as acyclic. The problem only arises because there are so many networks which contain feedback
that it seems hard to understand.

The body is experienced from within in a spatial manner, even though we also here can say that there is a
distance which the signals will travel from the receptors in the peripheral nervous system to the parts of the
brain where the signals are understood and interpreted. There are also somatic experiences where one wonders
whether the sensations are coming from that part of the body or are being projected onto that position in the
body. Bodily experience is at the core of Goenka vipassana and continuous up-and-down body scans while sitting
still gives rise to awareness of detailed pressure and tingling around the body, especially in the face for me.
In this process a part of perception is decomposed into smaller constituents. It is claimed that when following
this practice one will gain insight into the impermanence which marks existence since all sensation has its
background in change. Furthermore, by accepting and understanding this impermanence, one is led to let go of
attachment to these impermanent phenomena. Still, it is not completely clear to me how strong the connection
between awareness of bodily change corresponds to awareness of impermanence at other levels. One aspect is the
idea that there is a mouch stronger connection between thoughs, moods and other things in the domain of the mind 
and the subtle changes in the body. Feelings of arousal by the thought of a girl and reversely thinking of a
girl after otherrelated activity in some part of the body. this is what might be called the psychosomatic
perspective on vipassana, and I am unsure to what degree it is my own interpretation.

The breath is a central rhythm. It is the object of meditation in anapanasati where it is not controlled but
only perceived as it is. In yogic practice, pranayama as described by Patanjali is understood by fx Maharshi
to involve conscious, or rather willful, regulation deliberately to calm the mind. Maharshi describes a kind
of mystical connection between the breath and the mind which my cultural background is too far removed from to
understand, just like his description of the Heart. Personally, I do not experience any simple linear correlation
between breath and mind in the sense that a subtle breath would result or correlate with subtle mind and
detailed concentration. Actually I have not found anything, which works as a clear factor in the results of my
sessions. It is interesting that the breath is the object of meditation, since it sisvery far removed from being
an object or entity. Goenka comments on the fact that the breath is more visibly changing and that each inhalation
and exhalation has its own details, it can be short or long, subtle or strong, it can be focused predominatly
in one nostril, it is colder on the way in than the way out. The breath is aprocess, the breath is a rhythm, it
will end one day, just as it started once, it is impermanent. It connects the body to the environment directly
and continually, openly denying any strong separation and demarcation. It is a symbol of pure flow. It is
fundamental to combustion, yet it holds limited energy. It is arbitrary, because some organisms do not breathe
like we do, or we might have had multiple throats. The breath is a means for working with momentary awareness
because it constitutes a rhythm where the mind can always check in and register its awareness and presence.

I am eating one meal a day, yesterday, today and hopefully more days. I want to do it as an experiment: I have
felt as if though I have been too dependent on food as an activity and as something to satify craving and desire
which was not at core related to food. In general, the exam period was not healthy in terms of food and I spent
a lot of money under the personal excuse that I did not have time and that spending the money out was a forms of
investment. It has to be acknowledged that moderation of food and fasting which is essentially what I am doing
on a limited scale is a part of ascetic and spritiual practice. Putting a healthy amount of stress on the system
and at the same time reducing the stress which comes from the digestive system having to work and extended
period throughout the day is presumably evening out if not being better for the body. It is more for mental and
spiritual reasons I want to do it though. I hope that the pain and suffering which is unproblematic will be 
something to work with mentally, and hopefully one might be able to engage with or work on aspects or desires
which as mentioned might be coped with by eating. There is an interesting discussion to be had regarding the
physical and the mental: If I do not get food I might or will get irritated, as is common for almost everyone.
Being irritated or frustrated is obviously not an optimal state. It is possible to believe that this state or
mentality can be worked with in a spiritual manner in order to find deeper structures and details of this
frustration. Our goal should not merely be to solve the symptoms, irritability, by finding the physical solution,
eating. Still, there is a time for both. Now that I have vacation and have no responsibility and have few social
interactions, is a better time to work on these things than on a normal day.

What are we seeking? Happiness, peace or something third? I believe that even though the different spiritual
traditions might still be lacking in theory and practice, they have a message which is inherent in the word
spiritual: It is possible to find a deep happiness and peace independently of material circumstances. This
is the weak position. Many perspectives will go further and say that satisfaction cannot be found in matter
and only in spirit. Lastly but in strong connection with this is the idea that spirit is inherently blissful
and that it is only clinging to the ordinary desires of the material world which causes dissatisfaction,
despair and fear. One can certainly go too deep in this perspective if one denies that we as human beings have
fundamental needs which are also needed for spiritual practice. It is simply a reality that hunger in the
extreme can be such a distraction that one will not have the peace to develop one's mental capacities. More
theoretically, and injury to the brain would be able to cause severe loss of mindfulness for example. The
general healthy spiritual perspective will however note that the physical neds of human beings are extremely
limited and thus the problem is that most of the things we believe to be needs and not just pleasures and
luxuries are not really needs. The spiritual perspective introduces an unintuive notion of completeness into
life, in which the life and death of the body is not to be worried about and in which any worry for the past
and the future is wholly unfounded. This could be seens as a form of self-neglect and naivity, but in all cases
it is the result of some form of transcendence. The disattachement of the spirit from the body does not
necessarily involve a belief in a soul which cannot die, even though this is certainly often the case, nor does
the abstainence from worrying about tommorrow need to be dependent on belief in a god which will take care of
the physical circumstances. However, there does often seem to be some kind of metaphysical idea underlying the
spiritual expression. I believe that some are stronger than others and that there is no reason to expect that
one needs to adobt any dubious metaphysics or sacrifice rationality or sound science and skepticism. There is
however a core as mentioned, which will be needed, a way in which the seeker will be able to transcend the
clinging to personal life on which most desires rest and thus establish desirelessness and independent happiness.

Are we not longing for the perfect moment? The dramatic and beautiful classical pieces like Barber's Adagio
for strings provoke in me, that is in my body, movement and dynamicism which mirror a kind of importance.
Psychedelic experiences have provided the same feeling on a higher level of something extremely special.
The sacred has no closer meaning to me than this strong non-simplistic beauty which is expressed in master-
pieces like Gorecki's third symphony. Here this strong importance has no onesidedness in terms of happiness,
instead its power comes from the tension which makes it hard to ascribe postivity and bliss to it, yet there
is a clear sense in which one still believes it to be good. This goodness exist by incorporating evil and sin
into a golden symphonic fractal in which actual difference appears. Thus it shows us the paradoxicality of
existence where the bad things we really do not want could not be nonexistent. That all matter and phenomena
and life appears in difference and that this difference is in some sense more marvellous that pure unity.

I conjecture that mindfulness and concentration takes physical energy, that there is work being done. Is
this by mitrocondial combustion? Is it hormonal production? When I smoked cannabis I thought about what
kind of input it is. It has no calories, there is however calories from bonds in the tobacco and cannabis.
Combustion happens outside with a lighter lighting the joint. This lighter has gas with a high number
of joules, high energy density. The effect is that the results from the reaction, the gas with a certain
aggregation of different molecules. They arrive in the loung as an alternative to the normal composition of
molecules in the air in which oxygen is the normal desired subset. Here there is CO2 even. But one must not
forget the temperature which is massively higher. I venture that this temperature means higher entropy and
that this entropy should be understood as information, the inhaled gas has the ability to assert energy onto
the cells in the mouth, throat, lungs and even blood. It is to be understood as a large wave and this will also
mean influence on the molecular biology of the cell and its DNA.

What is stress and from which perspective do we get the most general description of stress? There is a force
against some physical body which has a certain area, mass and surface. When human beings excert force to lift
something, a vector inverse to gravity will have to be excerted, in order to increase the distance between
the weight and the earth. What is the earth? It is a composition of molecules and atoms with specific
temperatures excerting forces in different directions. A giant moving soup with a high energy activity burning
at the core. It is also some kind of vector fiedl. Each atom has a physical position in some newtonian space,
we then have a variety of properties which we can assign to either atoms, and downwards or upwards. There is
a clear topology of this movement. It is obvious in the mountains, the volcanic eruptions, tornados, climate
changes, weather patterns. I have moved from stress now. Stress is physical but it is also cellular,
physiological, anatomical, neural and psychological and social. But I would like to try to make it a fluent
and smooth movement of abstraction. Stress should eventually be understood in relation to suffering at a
spiritual level, dukkha.

There is supposedly a party at the computer science department. I believe that social interaction is a
massively energy consuming process and I believe that all work excerts stress, this stress is going in the
direction from the brain to the rest of the body. It is taxing. I do not believe in alcohol just as I wish
I had or will begin to believe that cannabis at least as smoked is not something to believe in. I have
perhaps some idea that spiritual practice with meditation and fasting is a very low energy state in which
a minimal stress or activity is sought. There is still stress however. On the knees from sitting in a good
posture, and thus it takes work. Likewise energy is excerted, as I have argued, in the pursuit of concentrated
states. How is it that fasting should be compatible with that? What about pranayama, breath retention: There
might be less oxygen because the breathing is so deep. Why would it otherwise be the case that we gasp for air
when we run but eventually it settles when we no longer wwill have to perform the activity centered on the
legs? It seems interesting that one can both believe increased energy consumption happens in thinking and in
the concentration needed in the meditation. What about looking at it with physical exercise as a model: You
excert force and activate the mitrocondrial combustion and other molecular reactions, you then pause after
some workout. The result is that stress has been induced and adaptation will occur as a procss. In response
to the stimuli and destruction of cells and general heating which causes breaking of bonds, a constructive
process occurs, anabolism, a builup. Thus we have during the workout stress correlating with work, but is not
also the repair a energy consuming process, in which resources will have to be distributed, proteins will have
to be created and cell division will need to occur. This work being done is happening at a much slower rate
however, within the general capacity of energy that the body has, unlike the workout which is completely
unsustainable. Is it the same thing with meditation?

There is a distinction between jhanic concentration which can only be archieved in a stable, resting posture,
an anana, and the moment to moment awareness of the contents of consciousness as might be had during walking
meditation and eventually as a general part of life activity. The first is based at least initially on
maintaining one-pointedness of mind on and object while mindfulness is independent of any specific object and
does not in principle require a lack of thought, if just one can be aware that one is thinking while one is
doing it. We believe very often that there should be effects of a meditation session on the activity of the mind
outside the session, a carrying over. If this is the case, then what is happening? If some network in the brain
has been engaged actively, in the sitting, in order to perform the work it takes to stay concentrated on an
object, then this network will presumably have a resulting adaptation in the process afterwards. Should we then
expect our general concentration to be a bit weaker afterwards and then see it grow as the network adapts? The
network or networks I am speaking of is regulatory feedback-based neural circuitry which allows some part of
the cognitive system to have knowledge of its own state in the manner previously discussed and the state
concerns what object is in focus and which thoughts and images have just appeared within the last couple of
seconds. It is still claimed by fx Maharshi, however, that yogis will be able to stay in jhanic states almost
indefinitely and this is obviously a strong point against the model of excercise and adaptation. An idea could
be to view the practice involved in developing the actual concentration skills as an energy intensive process
which builds up strength - Maharshi calls concentration a form of strength, actually - and when the neural
circuitry has sufficient strength it will be ablte to sustain the activity for a prolonged amount of time.
Now, here it would be appropriate to start discussing the distinction between endurance and strength. Strength
is to be understood approximately as the maximal capacity of force which one can excert over a very small window
of time, while endurance is concerned with the length of the window in which one can do work at a given intensity.
It seems that endurance seen as a functional mapping from intensity to timespan is monotonically decreasing and
that strength is then some upper part of the integral of this function. My point is that endurance is in some
sense more general than strength. There are muscles like the abdomen and heart, where endurance is indefinite
within the lifetime of the individual in most cases. Most spiritual practitioners will have the experience that
there is a dynamics of presence in the sitting, and outside, and that the presence cannot be sustained
indefinitely. Enlightenment is conceived as a state in which this presence is not lost. I do not claim that the
following is the case, only a playing with thoughts, but if we adopt such a simple model of enlightenment, then
we can see the phased dynamics of presence in the unenlightened as processes of work and repair while the
enlightened has established a neural structure which just as the heart has sufficient strength to uphold
indefinite endurance. This is not a final answer because there is a multitude of questions which have not been
answered: What exactly is this work which is being performed? How does it relate to self-reference and non-
duality? What would the initiation of indefinite sustenance mean in relation to enlightenment experiences? Just
as one will acknowledge that the phase space of ordinary and altered states of mind is extremely complex in its 
structure, so enlightenment could very well be a term describing a host of different areas. Before such a
conceptualisation would be meaningful one would need to present an initial notion of isomorphism between brains
and minds of different individuals.

has a strong likeness to electricity conceptually; it feels very structural, like a lightning which branches
fractally and symmetrically. On edibles this internal experience has been more organic and less detailed.

Senere:

Which energies move in us? When do they call for action, for care, for redemption and transcendence? When and
why do beauty lift its phase and face, spreading the creative movements and melodies in our bodies and throats?
There is nothing left to do but to feel this and to be this, the majestic and glorious Experience. The question
of ethics is interesting in relation to spirit. In Theravada Buddhism, moral conduct is a part of the path and
a basic necessity in order to gain sucess when it comes to the non-ethical parts of the path, at least according
to Goenka. Is ethics not simple, as all religions and paths willl have requirements for behavior. My question
comes from the perspective of non-duality. If one views all of reality as a unified whole where time is simply
a part, and this oneness is deemed perfect, then it seems natural to ask whether moral action has any meaning
and also whether utilitarian goals as expressed in effective altruism is meaningful. In buddhism there is not
inherently such a judgement of perfection as I am presenting it, rather experience is never an abstract totality
neither is being and so experience and life is what appears and suffering appears. In this view freedom is not
present but hidden, instead it exists in desirelessness and is maintained in desire. Desire however, in some
traditions is maintained by ignorance, but this is not ignorance of some total non-dual truth but an ignorance
which is very personal in structure, it is the inability to see the impermanence, the great flow, which is
present in our mode of thinking and being in the world.

There could be two kinds of morality: Morality as a code, the law as Saint Paul would say, which is external
to the human being not necessarily in an ontological sense but in the sense that it is received, learned and
followed as rules by the seeker and the person who aims for the virtuous life. The other morality is not law
but spirit in the sense that it is not defined by generality but internally in full coherence with the inner
bliss, it is the flowing of love for all the contents of experience which manifests itself not by pursuit or
moral striving, as the law would encourage, but as a release and falling down into the power which holds all
beings and their suffering. There is no way a spiritual insight or development will forget suffering or
diminish the importance of suffering, no way in which suffering will become less real. Once or as the ego
leaves the life there should be a natural connection with earth and society in such a way that compassion
spreads from the source towards any other being. The spiritual pursuit has as its basic fuel a self-compassion
which has not yet realised its full power but which is none the less active: Suffering and unsatisfaction
cannot and should not be understood abstractly and intellectually. No, suffering is experienced.

Does all action imply dissatisfaction? I am doing something because I have a preference for the world being
in some state which it is not currently in. If I take a sip of water it is because there is some preference
for drinking water, having the water in my body, removing thirst. We are not trying to renounce our needs or
preferences, we are not saying that you should not want something else. What are we then saying? That in all
action which you perform, you should be mindful of the action you are performing, the goal you are trying to 
fulfill and the desire you are trying to still. In perceiving the desire you should be mindful that since the
result will be a material one, it will not be fundamentally fulfilling and no matter how many actions you
perform in body and mind, the fundamental goal of final satisfaction will not be met. Only work in the spirit
can have effect on your deepest satisfaction, belonging and peace. This is the message of all sages.

A strong increase in my motivation to meditate and pursue the spiritual path has occured in me by actually
reading some books and realising that there are relatively clear goals which can be archieved on the way
to awakening which I am now quite certain is a real thing with a neural correlate. I have read Shinzen's
The Science of Enlightenment and am now reading Ingram. I am fascinated with how both of them speak of
impermanence on an attentional level in which reality is perceived stroboscopically in terms of very short
arisings and passings of sensorial phenonmena. Now that I articulate it I am not able to convey how significant
I regarded and still regard learning about this. I had the same thought as I had during my Goenka retreat:
I previously thought I had a pretyy clear grasp of the general landscape of things to know even though I do
not know them in depth, but this thing just seems to have gone under my nose. Why have I not previously heard
enlightenment and deep meditational attainment described from this phenomenological perspective? Fx Ingram will
say something like that all cognition or consciousness consists of a flickering event of sensorial followed
by a mental knowing of that experience, or "basic dharma theory tells us me I can't focus on two fingers at
once". What this tells me is that buddhist psychology deserves more of my attention and that experimental
psychology while totally valid clearly has limiations that can be complemented with these kinds of things.
I have been practicing noting of the six sense doors heavily while biking with my grandfather and I feel that
I have gained a lot from it and that some aspect of my concentration ability has improved with insight into how
fast my consciousness is changing thus giving a new perspective on the task of trying to hold attention on one
thing. Attention is not so much held on one thing and some time moving away (on my level), as continually
moving, flickering but with an acceptable number of frames being the object, my nose, an its is rather this
frequency which has to be maintained.

The Mahasi noting technique on the level at which I currently understand it is to make a mental verbal note
of 'hearing', 'seeing', 'feeling', 'smelling', 'tasting' and 'thinking' every time a sensation appears in
awareness. By doing this, one can increase mindfulness by developing a better clarity and understanding through
a reductionistic approach in which the general experience is broken down into smaller pieces. It also has the
effect of developing concentration, because one will forget to do this nothing, if one is not concentrated.
Even though one were very fast at doing this noting, one would presumably only note a fraction of the sensory
experiences (even though I do not know what one might be capable of) I don't think that his is a proble, and
will be maladaptive for cognition. I think that the practice can be understood by analogy with machine learning
classification problems. By doing noting, one is providing the brain with data points which allows it to learn to
discriminate at a higher level between sensorial signals. Even though there is probably already a distinction
between the senses at a lower level of processin, by using language to note these sensorial experiences, one
establishes this ability at a higher level close to consciousness. But one can play multiple of these noting
games, in order to train multiple discriminatory abilities and thus develop a wider and more powerful
reductionistic mindfulness. For example, I have been practicing a classification where I note P for a physical
sensate signal and M for a the mental image or thought which arises as the inference of that signal. For
example I could hear some sound and note P and then since I believe that the sound is the sound of rain, I note
M for this mental concept of rain. I do not need to be clear about what my judgment (rain) is, just that some
kind of inference is happening. I could also see some white and black, note P for this sensorial data and note
P because this white and black is understood as a word on a piece of paper. By practicing this classification
one is only noting a fraction of all these perceptions but they are providing data to develop the ability to
distinguish between these two aspects of experience. It does not even matter, I think, that perhaps this
distinction is simplified because the actual mechanics are much more complex with regard to perceiving objects.
It would be impossible to have awareness of all the details of low level processing in consciousness, because
that would require a kind of duplication or mirroring at higher levels. Still, there is still at good reason to
increase the ability to understand one's cognition, and this is also the basis for psychotherapies like
metacognitive behavioral therapy.

We can make a simple model of concentration in which awareness is a discrete signal with a high sample rate, for
imagination say 300. Each frame can correspond to a small sensation such as a single wavelet of a bird sound or
a mental image of a relative or anything else. Since it is not helpful to view meditational ability,
concentrational ability, as a monolith, we can propose various aspects of training with this model. When Culadasa
describes following the breath and being mindful of the 4 phases; in, out and the two pauses, he is aksing one
to register sensations 4 times in one breath. A breath's length varies so there is not a specific frequency, but
the idea is that one can train to have at least 1 noting of the meditational object per second, one hertz. If
one does not have that, it is counted as a break of a streak and we then want to maximize the streaks and
minimize the number of breaks, which now has a formal definition. We might want to have a description of streak
starting such that we avoid multiple countings of a break caused by the difficulty of going back to the object.
I don't know whether a metronome is beneficial for actually doing this, or whether it is more just a model.
With 60 bpm, one beat per second, it is possible to notice the nose just after the beat and still have time
to notice other things. There is clearly a notion of endurance because it is easier to be motivated to complete
one minute without a break than 15 minutes. Just like in guitar and general instrument practice there could be
some standard for when you would be ready to increase the bpm. In guitar practice I have heard teachers say up
and down 5 times, roughly 16 * 2 * 5 = 160, so perhaps 3 minutes would be fit. The difference is however that
unlike in guitar practice we actually care that we should be able to hold it indefinitely, almost. It is difficult
to evaluate whether a noting has occured between to beats. Either the policy should be that one should choose a
specific noticing out of the many which might occur or one should simply validate at each beat that at least one
noting occured in the previous gap.

Sound. Hearing is an important sense door for me, because it is easier to be aware of the vibratory character of
experience here. A sound as a wave with many subwaves which can be heard within it. Interference can be revelatory
because it allows multiple signals to exist toegether and it is up to awareness to decide which one to tune into.
As practice continues each sound is revealed as a specific wave in the space of other waves and so it integrates
into the general form of experience. As noted, the importance of LSD is this integration in which the senses
collapse into one plane, and even though I have not clearly seen this, the information moving on this plane is
then waves. Does it make sense to listen to the sound of me writing, this sentence, it can seem absurd to notice
the small flickerings of the paper, is this bound to lead to some kind of overstimulation? I have a kind of faith
thath it is not so; that if done in a controlled manner, it is precisely what insight practice is. Every action
or moment or thought is a chance to try this integration and ask: How is this sensation simply a sensation like
all others? Can you break the process of writing down, such that you will be able to notice each small part of
writing the sentence, words, letters and subparts of the characters? Some characters like s is one smooth movement,
unlike i or t which (k) consist of two. Even the letters which are continuous are not being written in a single
moment, so insight practice of writing consist in breaking this movement into multiple pieces. I don't know if it
is just my way of writing but it requires a lot of effort for me to write and this too can be investigated: Where
exactly? Which frequency is it? Look in your mind at how the hand moves and how the pencil moves. Try not to
identify or disidentify with the hand or the pen or the ink. All of it is simply happening and your job is to look
at exactly what is happening. Notice for example that your desk is not completely stable; energy flows in waves
throughout the table out into the universe. When you are doing all of this there is a kind of flow and ease to
the marvellous process of writing which really involves many complex processes of cognition which will not be
apparent to you. These too can be investigated. Instead of being in the realm of the physical world corresponding
to the five sense doors of hearing, seeing, tasting, smelling and feeling, we are now investigating the sense
door of thinking. The first stage of insight as described in Ingram's MCTB, which I am currently reading, is called
knowledge of Mind and Body. Which mental sensations or experiences can we identify in writing? There is an
appearance of the word I am going to write in my mind before I am performing the action of writing. This is an
interesting thing to try to observe. But there are also times when we go further than that: We are not simplistic
Markov chains. Sometimes this larger planning is simply to plan to write a phrase or a set of words, some times it is
a complete sentence like 'sometimes it is a complete sentence'. When doing so the sentence will be kept in
working memory and perhaps this can be investigated too: The multiple rehearsings or repetitions of the sentence.
There is also the fact that when a larger sentence has been planned there is capacity to plan the next sentence,
and this planning conceptual at least for me. It is as if though it happens at the level of concepts and even
images and then there is a process in which this thought or idea will be transformed to the linear format of
language. The following was a quite long sentence and fx the concept linear was appearing in my mind and some 
consideration or image of placing words first and then filling the gaps between. Still it seems as if though
there is more structure to complex sentences than simply filling gaps. Other mental events are the higher level
moving, planning, where a specific paragraph or idea has been explored at the level of multiple sentences. I
just found that I then remembered a larger idea that I had before but had to put to the side and then I can pick
it up later. If we have a too simplistic view of short and long term memory, we might not be able to fully
understand this.

Even though log writing might have reasonable coherence as I believe this session has had, I do not have any
overall goal and thus there is a pronounced lack of progress. It seems as if though such a larger cohesion is
often enabled by writing a plan for the text, perhaps because of limitations to human memory.

My concentration has improved. Something which has really helped me today, I believe, is to have the five
hindrances, namely desire, aversion, agitation, dullness and doubt in mind when practicing concentration. It
seems to me that most distractions are of two kinds, discomforb and thinking about past and future. I view
discomfort as a kind of aversion and when faced with this distraction I focus intensely on a single point at the
tip of my nose, as if though piercing with high sped through it. Currently, I feel it as a kind of acceleration
and actual acceleration in a car, because I felt today as if though travelling really fast, almost as on a space
ship. This piercing through is the application of effort in order to tighten the concentration, a zoooming in
which thereby removes distractions of discomfort from view. When doing this acceleration I try to continue with
if for a couple of seconds and listen to the state of my body. If during or after the acceleration the sense
sphere of the mind has high activity with images of people or thoughts trivial or intellectual are present, I
view it as a kind of dulnlness in which there are phenomena in the mind which are more interesting than the nose.
In that case I want to engage with the nose, not as a point but as a whole nose with movement, change, pressures,
pins-and-needles and any kind of dynamic activity, gross or subtle. Depending on whether the distractions are of
the two kinds just described, I will choose either remedy. Distractions which are uninteresting physical phenomena
I will regard as dullness also. Agitation in the form of worry, anxiety and similar feelings I will attend to by
diminishing the onepointedness and relax my effort. All of this is only tested in a limited scope and I have much
to learn but I feel that it is in line with the tachings in The Mind Illuminated and Joseph Goldstein's
Mindfulness.
